13 & 14 GEO . 5.-A.D. 1923
:
1.An Act forthe continuanceof ChargingPowers in respectof Canal
or InlandNavigationUndertakingsinNorthern Irelandof which
possessionwas retainedor taken by the Ministryof Transport
under the Ministryof Transport Act , 1919. (Canals Continu-
ance of Charging Powers.)
2. An Act to authorisethe employment of additionalInspectorsfor
the purposes of Weights and Measures Acts, 1878 to 1919.
(Inspectorsof Weightsand Measures.)
3. An Act to applycertainSums out of the ConsolidatedFund of
Northern Irelandto the serviceof the period ended on the
thirty-firstday ofMarch ,nineteenhundred and twenty -two ,and
of the years ending on the thirty-firstday of March , nineteen
hundred and twenty-three, and the thirty-firstday of March,
nineteenhundred and twenty-four, and to make furtherprovi.
sionwith respectto the appropriationof certainsuppliesgranted
by Parliament for the serviceof the year ending on the thirty-
firstday of March , nineteenhundred and twenty-three. (Con-
solidatedFund and Appropriation .)
4. An Act to provide for the applicationof creditbalancesin the
Exchequer of Northern Ireland; to charge certainsums upon
the Consolidated Fund of Northern Ireland ; to extend the
powers ofthe MinistryofFinance with respectto CapitalMoneys
and the making of Loans ; to amend the Law with respectto
the preparation, examination and presentationto Parliament
of Accounts; and for purposesconnectedtherewith. (Ex-
chequerand FinancialProvisions.)
5. An Act to amend the PettySessionsClerk(Ireland) Act, 1858,
and the Dogs 'Regulation(Ireland)Act,1865,in theirapplication
to NorthernIreland. (PettySessionsFeesand Administration.)

7. An Act to amend the Law relatingto Promissory Oaths in its
applicationto NorthernIreland. (PromissoryOaths.)
8. An Act to amend the law in Northern Irelandwith respectto
offencesagainstpersonsunder the age of sixteen, and with
respectto penaltiesunder sectionthirteenof the CriminalLaw
Amendment Act , 1885. (Criminal Law Amendment .)
9. An Act to amend the Law of Evidence in itsapplicationto Nor-
thern Ireland. (Criminal Evidence.)
10. An Act to amend the Law with respectto Road Expenditure in
Northern Ireland, and the procedure in connectiontherewith.
(LocalGovernment (Roads).)
11. An Act to amend the provisionsof the Unemployment Insurance
Acts (NorthernIreland),1920to1922,relatingtospecialperiods,
theperiodof benefitand the conditionsforthe receiptof benefit,
to provide for continuingthe existingratesof benefitand for
making consequentialalterationsin the ratesof contributions,
to increasethe totalamount of advances which may be made
by the MinistryofFinanceforthe Northern Irishunemployment
fund, and otherwiseto amend the said Acts. (Unemployment
Insurance .)
12. An Act tomake provisionfortheclosingon Sunday and Christmas
Day ofcertainpremiseslicensedforthesaleofintoxicatingliquor,
the abolitionof certain off-licences,and the settlement of claims
for compensation arisingthereout; to impose restrictionson
the saleof methylated spirits; and to amend the law relating
to the saleand supply of intoxicatingliquorby retail; and for
purposesconnected therewith. (IntoxicatingLiquor.)
13. An Act to amend the Representationof the PeopleAct , 1918,in
itsapplicationto the Local Government Franchisesin Northern
Ireland. (LocalGovernment (Franchise).)
14. An Act to givethe forceofLaw to theconsentof theGovernment
of Northern Ireland to certainarrangements for Reliefin respect
of Double Taxation as between Northern Ireland and the Irish
Free State. (Double TaxationRelief.)
15. An Act to amend sectionone ofthe Loans GuaranteeAct (Northern
Ireland), 1922. (Loans Guarantee(Amendment ).)
16. An Act to continue, as respectsNorthern Ireland, the Increase
ofRent and Mortgage Interest(Restrictions)Act,1920,untilthe
twenty-fourthday of December ,nineteenhundred and twenty-
three. (Increase of Rent and Mortgage InterestRestrictions
(Continuance).)
17.An Act to regulatethe disposalof by-productsof flaxscutching
at Scutch Millsin Northern Ireland,and the conduct ofbusiness
in connectionwith flaxscutching. (ScutchMills.)

furtherSuppliesgrantedin thisSessionof Parliament. (Appro-
priation (No. 2.).)

2),and to amend the SuperannuationActs (NorthernIreland),
1921 and 1922. (Superannuation.)
29. An Act to enable certainspecialconstablesto be appointed as
members oftheRoyalUlsterConstabulary. (Constabulary.)

CHAPTER 1.
Act for the continuance of Charging Powers in
respect of Canal or Inland Navigation Under-
takings in Northern Ireland ofwhich possession
was retainedor taken by the Minister ofTrans-
port under the Ministry of Transport Act ,1919 .
[29th March, 1923.]

• and the Senate and the House of Commons of
thern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
I by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
1.-(1)In thecaseofcanalorinlandnavigationunder-

inedortakenby theMinisterofTransportunderthe
vers contained in sectionthree of the Ministry of
nsport Act, 1919, paragraph(e) of sub-section(1)

(3)Any applicationby the undertakersto theMin-
istryforthe purposesofthisAct shallbe accompanied
by such information, certifiedin such manner ,as the
Ministry may require,with respectto the financialposi-
tion of the undertaking in question; and beforemaking
an orderupon such applicationthe Ministryshallrequire
the undertakersto give publicnoticeof the application,
and as to the manner in which , and the time within
which , representationsto the Ministry may be made ;
and the Ministry shallconsiderany representations
which shallbe duly made .
(4) Before making an order under thisAct, the
Ministry may appoint an officeror other person to in-
quire into and report upon the circumstancesaffecting
theundertakinginquestion(includingthematterofany
applicationor representationsmade to the Ministry) in
such manner and aftersuch publicnoticeas the Ministry
may direct.
Such officeror person shallhear such witnesses
and callforsuchdocuments and accounts as he thinksfit,
and shallhave power to take evidence on oath and for
that purpose to administeroaths.
(5) The costsincurredby theMinistryinconnection
with any such inquiry, includingthe remuneration,at
such rateas the Ministrymay determine,of the officer
or otherpersonappointedto holdthe inquiry,shallbe
paid by the undertakersor such otherpartiesto the
inquiryastheMinistrymay determine,and theMinistry
may certifythe amount of the costsincurred, and any
sums so certifiedand directedby the Ministryto be
paid by any persons shallbe a debt to the Ministry
from such persons.

4.-(1)The saidMinistryofFinance may borrow from
any person,by theissueofTreasuryBillsor otherwise,on、
the creditof the aforesaidsums , any sum or sums not
exceedinginthe whole one millionpounds .
(2) The date of payment of any Treasury Bills
issued under this section shall be a date not later than
the thirty-firstday of March , nineteen hundred and
twenty -four.
(3)Any money borrowed otherwise than on
TreasuryBillsshallbe repaid, with any interestdue
thereon,out of the growing produce of the said Consoli-
dated Fund at any date not laterthan the quarternext
succeedingto that in which the money was borrowed .
(4)Any money borrowed under thissectionshallbe
placed to the creditof the account of the Exchequer of
Northern Ireland,and shallform part ofthe saidConsoli-
dated Fund ,and be availableinany manner inwhich such
Fund is available .

of the saidMinistryof Finance, be appliedin defraying
any expenditureforthe purposesofthe SpecialConstabu-
larywhich isnot provided for in the sums appropriated
forthelast-mentionedpurposes.
6. This Act may be citedas the ConsolidatedFund
and AppropriationAct (Northern Ireland), 1923.

An Act to amend the Law relatingto Promissory
Oaths in itsapplicationto Northern Ireland.
B
[10th May ,1923.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of North-
ern IrelandinthispresentParliament assembled,and by
the authorityofthe same ,as follows:-
1.-(1) Every person who isat the passing of this
Act either-
(a) an officerservinginan establishedcapacityin
the civil service of the Government of Northern
Ireland ; or
(b) otherwiseemployed on fulltime dutiesinorby
any department or by any authority of that
Government
shall,beforethe firstday of July,nineteenhundred and
twenty -three, or before such laterdate as may in any
specialcasebe allowedby the Ministryof Finance for
Northern Ireland,and every person who afterthe passing
of this Act is admitted to serve as such an officer, or is
taken into such employment as aforesaid, shall, within
one month afterhe isso admitted or taken intoemploy-
ment,takean oathintheformprescribedby theSchedule
to this Act
(2)Without prejudicetothe power ofany otherper-
sons to administeran oath,the oath by thisAct required
to be taken may be administeredto the personsrequired
to take the same by any Resident MagistrateinNorthern
Ireland,or by the permanent head of the department to
which the personrequiredto take the oath belongs,or by
such other superiorofficersof the department as the
permanent head thereofmay designatefor the purpose,
such permanent head or other superiorofficersbeing
themselves officersservingin an establishedcapacity in
the said civilservice who have taken such oath .
(3)For the purpose ofsecuringcompliance with the
requirementsof thisAct ,a recordshallbe kept by every
department or authorityof the saidGovernment of the
personsby whom the oath istaken under thisAct .

An Act to amend the law in Northern Ireland with
respect to offencesagainst persons under the age
ofsixteen,and with respect to penaltiesunder
section thirteen of the Criminal Law Amend-
ment Act , 1885 . [10th May , 1923.]
B E itenactedby the King'smost ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same , as follows:-
1. It shallbe no defence to a charge or indictment
foran indecentassaulton a childor young person under
the age ofsixteentoprove thathe or she consentedto the
act of indecency.
2. Reasonable causeto believethat a girlwas of or
above the age ofsixteenyears shallnot be a defenceto a
charge under sub-section(1) of sectionfive or under
section six of the Criminal Law Amendment Act , 1885
(in thisAct referredto as " the principalAct "). The
limitof time mentioned in the second provisoto section
fiveofthe principalAct ,as amended by sectiontwenty-
seven ofthe Preventionof Crueltyto ChildrenAct,1904,
shall be nine months after the commission of the offence .
3. Any person who isconvictedofan offenceagainst
sectionthirteenof the principalAct (which relatesto
summary proceedingsagainstbrothelkeepers, & c.) shall
be liableon summary conviction-
(a) toa finenot exceedingone hundred pounds or
to imprisonment with or without hard labour
for a term not exceeding three months ; and
:
(b) on a second or subsequentconviction,to a fine
not exceedingtwo hundred and fiftypounds or
to imprisonment with or without hard labour
for a term not exceeding six months ;
or,in any such case,to both fineand imprisonment.

An Act to amend the Law of Evidence in its
application to Northern Ireland .
B
[10th May ,1923.]
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled
and by the authorityof the same as follows:-
1. Every person charged with an offence, and the
wife or husband , as the case may be, of the person so
charged shallbe a competent witnessfor the defenceat
every stage of the proceedings, whether the person so
charged ischarged solelyorjointlywith any otherperson:
Provided as follows :-
(a) A person so charged shallnot be calledas a
witness in pursuance of thisAct except upon
hisown application:
(b) The failureof any person charged with an
offence, or of the wife or husband , as the case
may be of the person so charged,to give evi-
dence shallnot be made the subject of any
comment by the prosecution:
(c) The wifeorhusband ofthepersoncharged shall
not,save as inthisAct mentioned,be calledas
a witnessinpursuance ofthisAct except upon
the applicationof the person so charged :
(d) Nothing inthisAct shallmake a husband com-
pellableto discloseany communication made
to him by his wife during the marriage, or a
wife compellableto discloseany communica-
tion made to her by her husband during the
marriage :
(e) A person charged and being a witnessinpursu-
ance ofthisAct may be asked any questionin
cross-examination notwithstanding that it
would tend to criminate him as to the offence
charged :

## Page 39

WN W
pursuance ofthisAct shallnot be asked,and if
asked shallnot be requiredto answer, any
question tending to show that he has com-
mitted or been convicted of or been charged
with any offenceotherthan that wherewith he
isthen charged ,or isof bad character,unless-
(i) the proofthathe has committed or been
convicted of such other offence is admis-
sibleevidenceto show that he isguilty
of the offence wherewith he is then
charged ;
(ii) he has personallyor by his advocate
asked questionsof the witnessesforthe
prosecutionwith a view to establishhis
own good character, or has given evi-
dence ofhisgood character,orthe nature
or conduct of the defence is such as to
involveimputationson the characterof
the prosecutoror the witnessesfor the
prosecution ; or
(iii) he has given evidenceagainstany other
person charged with the same offence:
(g) Every personcalledas a witnessinpursuance
of thisAct shall, unlessotherwiseordered by
the court,give his evidence from the witness
box or other place from which the other wit-
nesses give their evidence :
(h) Nothing inthisAct shallaffecttheprovisionsof
sectionfourteenofthe Petty Sessions(Ireland)
Act , 1851, or any rightof the person charged
to make a statement without being sworn .

Evidence Act (Northern Ireland), 1923.

An Act tomake provisionforthe closingon Sunday
and ChristmasDay ofcertainpremiseslicensed
forthe saleofintoxicatingliquor, the abolition
ofcertainoff-licences,and the settlement ofclaims
for compensation arising thereout ; to impose
restrictionson the sale of methylated spirits;
and to amend the law relating to the sale and
supply of intoxicatingliquorby retail; and for
purposes connected therewith .

FIRST SCHEDULE .
PART I.
CONSTITUTION OF THE CLAIMS TRIBUNAL .
The ClaimsTribunal,when hearingor determininga claimunder
hisAct,shallbe constitutedofatleastthreeofthefollowingpersons--
(a) a recorderor county court judge ;
(b) a personnominatedby theMinisterofFinance;
(c) two personsnominated by the MinisterofHome Affairs,one
of whom isa residentmagistrate;
(d) a justice(not being a residentmagistrate) chosen by the
justicesfor a petty sessionsdistrict:
Providedthat no personwho isa member ofthe ClaimsTribunalinhis
apacityas recorder,county court judge, magistrateor justice,shall
ittohearordeterminea claim,unlessinthatcapacityhe hasjuris-
Lictionorhasbeenappointedforthe countyorpettysessionsdistrict
which the premisesaresituateinrespectof which theclaimismade .

PROVISIONS APPLICABLE TO CONSIDERATION OF
CLAIMS .

Artue ofthisAct ,to be renewable,the followingprovisionsshallapply

remises :

in the value of the premises to an amount not exceeding
five times the difference between the amount at which the
premises were valued under the IrishValuation Acts im-
mediately beforethey ceased to be licensedpremises and
the sum which the Commissioner of Valuation for Northern
Irelandcertifies,in such manner as may be prescribedby
rulesmade by the Ministryof Finance under thisAct ,to be
their annual value immediately after they ceased to be
licensed ;

have foreach ofthe threeyearsending5th April,1923,been
brought intocharge for assessmentunder the Income Tax
Act,1918,orany Act amendingthesame,compensationshall
be paid inrespectoflossofprofits,either-

catingliquor, to an amount not exceedingfive-thirds
of the averageannual profitsforthe saidthreeyearsso

PART II .
PROVISIONS AS TO REGISTERED CLUBS .
The RegistrationofClubs(Ireland)Act,1904,shallhave effectEdw .7 with the followingamendments :--
(1) Every applicationforan originalcertificateof registration
ofa clubshallbe made in the month ofJanuary inany year.
(2) The noticeofapplicationforregistrationofa certificateshall
bepublishedon some day notmore thanfourweeks,norless
thantwo weeks,beforethefirstday ofJanuaryinany year,

## Page 73

cate or a renewal thereof) shall, in additionto any other
publication, be publishedonce in the BelfastGazette.
(3) Without prejudiceto the provisionsof sectionnine of the
saidAct (which relatesto the cancellationof certificatesof
registration), every club whose certificateof registration
would,apartfrom thisparagraph,expireat any time after
thepassingofthisAct and beforethe thirty-firstday of
January,nineteenhundred and twenty-four,shallbe deemed
to remain registereduntilthe last-mentioned date,and the
certificateofregistrationof every club whose certificatewas
granted or renewed at any time afterthe thirty-firstday of
January,nineteenhundred and twenty-three,and beforethe
passingof thisAct shallexpireon the thirty-firstday of
January,nineteenhundred and twenty-four;and the certifi-
cateof registrationof every such club shallhave effect
accordingly.
(4) SectionfiveofthesaidAct shallhaveeffectasifinparagraph
(i)thewords " fiveyearsnext precedingthe formationofthe
club " were substituted for the words " twelve months next
precedingthe formationofthe club," and as ifthe reference
in that paragraph to the Licensing(Ireland)Acts,1833 to
1900 ,included a referenceto thisAct .
(5) Every registeredclub shallexhibitin a conspicuouspart of
the club premisesa statement,printedin plaintype,of the
hours during which intoxicatingliquormay be suppliedon
the premises,and the rulesof every registeredclub shallso
provide. Every personenteredin the registerofclubsas an
officialor member of the committee of management or gov-
erningbody ofany registeredclubwhich failsto comply with
the requirementsof thisprovisionshallbe liableon convic-
tionto a penaltynot exceedingthirtypounds,and thefailure
to comply with thoserequirementsshallbe a ground on
which objectionmay be taken totherenewalofthe certificate
of registrationof a club.
(6) For the purpose of any proceedingsunder the said Act ,a
court of summary jurisdictionshallbe constitutedof not
lessthan two residentmagistrates, and no justiceof the
peacenotbeinga residentmagistrateshallhave jurisdiction
to act on the hearingor in connectionwith any such pro-
ceedings .

of a yearlyvalue of not lessthan fivepounds ,
ora dwelling-house ;and

so occupied,eitherinthatarea or,ifthat area

borough, in any administrativecounty or

2.
An Act to give the force of Law to the consent of
the Government of Northern Ireland to certain
arrangements for Relief in respect of Double
Taxation as between Northern Ireland and the
Irish Free State . [22nd June , 1923.]
Whereas ,in pursuance of sub-section(4) (b) of sec-
tionfiveofthe IrishFree State(ConsequentialProvisions)
Act , 1922 (Session2), the Government of Northern Ire-
land has given itsconsent to the extensionto Northern
Ireland of the arrangements which are set forth, as so
extended,inthe Scheduleto thisAct,beingarrangements
made in pursuance of the saidsectionand specifiedin a
declarationof His Majesty in Councildated the twenty-
ninth day of March , nineteenhundred and twenty-three
(in this Act referredto as " the scheduled arrange-
ments ") :
And whereas the scheduled arrangements relateto
Estate Duty and Stamp Duties, which are taxes within
the powers of the Parliament of Northern Ireland, and
itisnecessarythat the said consent to the extensionof
the scheduled arrangements to Northern Irelandshould
have the force of law therein :
Be itthereforeenactedby theKing'smost Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresentParliament assembled,
and by the authorityofthe same ,as follows:-
1. The consentgiven by the Government ofNorth-
ern Irelandto the scheduledarrangements shallhave the
forceoflaw inNorthern Irelandasfrom the twenty-ninth
day of March nineteenhundred and twenty -three.
2. This Act may be citedas the Double Taxation
ReliefAct (Northern Ireland), 1923.
SCHEDULE .
Arrangements forReliefin respectofDouble Taxationas extended
to Northern Ireland .
PART II .
Estate Duty .
(a)Where theMinistryofFinanceforNorthernIrelandissatisfied
thatEstateDuty ispayableintheIrishFreeStateby reasonofa death

## Page 77

any
Stateand passingon suchdeath,thatMinistryshallallowa sum equal
to the amount ofthatduty to be deducted from the EstateDuty pay-
ablein Northern Irelandinrespectofthatpropertyon thesame death.
(6)Where the Revenue Commissionersofthe IrishFree Stateare
satisfiedthatEstateDuty ispayableinNorthernIrelandby reasonofa
deathofa persondyingon orafterthesaidfirstday ofAprilinrespect
ofany propertysituatein Northern Irelandand passingon such death,
they shallallowa sum equalto the amount ofthatduty to be deducted
from the EstateDuty payablein the IrishFree Statein respectofthat
property on the same death.
(c)Any questionas to whether any propertyisto be treatedfor
thepurposesofthisarrangement as situatedin Northern Irelandor in
the IrishFree State shallbe determined according to the laws in force
inIrelandon thesixthday ofDecember,nineteenhundredand twenty-
two .
(d) This arrangement shallapply as between Northern Ireland
and the Irish Free State until the Government of Northern Ireland
signifythat they have withdrawn theirconsentto such application.
PART III .
Stamp Duties .
(a) Where on or afterthe firstday of April,nineteenhundred
and twenty-three,an instrumentis chargeablewith Stamp Duty in
Northern Irelandand inthe IrishFree State,and has been stamped in
one of thosecountries,the instrumentshall,to the extentof the duty
itbears,be deemed to be stamped inthe othercountry :
Provided that,ifthe Stamp Duty chargeableon any instrument
in such othercountryexceedsthe Stamp Duty chargeableinrespectof
thatinstrumentin the countryin which the instrumenthas previously
beenstamped,theinstrumentshallnot be deemed tohave beenduly
stamped in such othercountryunlessand untilstamped in accordance
with the laws ofthatcountry with a stamp denotingan amount equal
to such excess .
(b)Where compositionforStamp Duty ismade or agreed to be
made in one of such countries,any instrumentwhich by virtueof the
compositionisexempt from the payment ofduty inthatcountryshall,
on and afterthe saidfirstday ofApril,be treatedinthe othercountry
as having been stamped in the first-mentioned country with a stamp
denotingthe amount of duty which,but forthe composition,would
have been chargeableon that instrument.
(c) This arrangement shallapply as between Northern Ireland
and the Irish Free State until the Government of Northern Ireland
signifythatthey have withdrawn theirconsentto such application.

flaxscutching at Scutch Millsin Northern Ire-
land , and the conduct of business in connection
with flaxscutching. [22nd June,1923.]
B E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Irelandin thispresent Parliament assembled,
nd by the authority of the same , as follows:-
1.- (1) It shallnot be lawfulforany person,being
he owner or having controlof a scutch mill-
(a) to demand or accept, or offerto accept, as
payment or part payment of charges for
scutching, any of the by -products of the pro-
cessof flaxscutching, or
(b) to purchase or attempt to purchase any ofthe
by -products of the processof flax scutching
beforethat processhas been carriedout.
(2) It shallbe the duty of every person, being the
wner or having controlof a scutch mill—
(a) to supply such suitableweighingappliances
forweighingtheproductsor by -productsofflax
scutchingas may be approved by or on behalf
of the Ministryof Agriculturefor Northern
Ireland(in thisAct referredto as " the Min-
istryof Agriculture");
(b) to keep a record of the scutching operations
in the form A set out in the Schedule to this
Act , or in a form to the like effect, and to
permit that record to be inspected, and ex-
tractstherefrom to be taken , at allreasonable
timesby an officeroforpersonduly authorised
in writingby the Ministry of Agriculture.
(c) to furnish, at the time of or priorto the de-
liveryof every lot of scutched flax, to the
owner thereofor hisauthorisedrepresentative
a statementin writingin the form B setout in
the Schedule to this Act , or in a form to the
like effect .
(d) to exhibit,ina prominentplaceon thepremi-
ses of the mill a statement showing whether or
not he has insured againstfire, while in the
Provisionsregulating

and allfinesthereunder shallbe recoveredon summary
convictionbefore a court of summary jurisdictionin
manner provided by the Summary Jurisdiction(Ireland)
Acts,and appealsfrom any such courtshalllieinaccord-
ance with the provisionsof the saidActs.
(3) Allfinesimposed under thisAct shallbe applied
inmanner directedby the FinesAct (Ireland),1851,and
any Act amending the same .
3.- (1) This Act may be citedas the Scutch Mills
Act (Northern Ireland), 1923.
(2) This Act shallcome intooperationon the first
day of August , nineteen hundred and twenty-three.

An Act to establish local authorities for education
in Northern Ireland ; to make betterprovision
therein as respects education ,school attendance ,
the employment of childrenand young persons,
the health and welfare of school children and
afflictedchildren,and the trainingand employ-
ment of school teachers; and for purposes
connected therewith . [22nd June , 1923.]
B
E itenacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Ireland in thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
PART I.
ADVISORY COUNCIL AND LOCAL AUTHORITIES AND
COMMITTEES .
1.-(1) For the purpose of advising the Ministry
of Education for Northern Ireland(in thisAct referred
to as " the Ministry") on educational matters, there
shallbe establishedan Advisory Council,whose members
shallbe appointed by the Ministerof Education forNor-
thern Ireland(inthisAct referredto as " the Minister" ),
and the Ministryshalltake intoconsiderationany advice
or representationsubmitted to it by the Advisory
Council .
(2) The constitutionand proceedingsofthe Council
shallbe regulatedfrom time to time by Minutes to be
made by the Minister and laid before both Houses of
Parliament :
Provided that-
(a) the Council shall consistof not more than
twenty-one members ,who shallhold officefor
such periods,not exceedingthreeyears,as the
Ministermay by any such Minute determine,
and who shallbe eligiblefor re-appointment ;

Minister ; and
(c) the Councilshallbe summoned by the Minister,
and shallmeet twice each year, and at such
othertimesas the Ministermay considerneces-
sary .

2.-(1) For the purposes of this Act the council
of each county and county borough shall be a local authorities
authority for education (in this Act referredto as an
" education authority" ) and the county or county
borough shall, forthosepurposes, form the education
area of the education authority.
(2) The powers and duties under thisAct of an
education authority, being the council of a county
borough,shall,except asrespectsthe raisingofmoney by
rateor loan, the generalcontrolof expenditure to such
extent as that controlmay be retainedby the educa-
tion authoritythemselves, and the acquisition, holding
or disposal of land, be exercised and performed
through an education committee of the council,
consistingof twenty -one members appointed by the
councileitherfrom the members of theirown body or
partlyfrom thosemembers and partlyfrom otherpersons,
as the council think fit.
The powers and dutiesof the councilof a county
borough as an education authority, other than those
requiredto be exercisedand performed through the edu-
cation committee, may be exercised and performed
through such committee consistingof members of the
council,and on such conditions,as the councilthink fit.

cation authority, not being the council of a county

PART IV .
HIGHER EDUCATION .
19. It shallbe theduty of the education authority
to takesuch steps(whether by the provisionofschools,or

the Ministry, to supply or aid the supply of higher
education and to promote the general co-ordinationof
all forms of education .
For thepurposesofthisAct,theexpression“ highereducation" means any form of education other than
elementary oragriculturaleducation,and includeseduca-
tion complying with regulationsof the Ministryand

(a) ata preparatoryschool,thatistosay,a school
ordepartment ofa schoolprovidinginstruction

intermediateor secondary school; or

deemed suitablefor pupils who , before en-
trance,have reached such stage(hereinafterin
thissectionreferredtoasthe "qualifyingstage")
of attainment in elementary educationas may
be prescribedby the Ministry; or
(c) at a secondary school,that isto say, a school
or department of a school providing at least
a fiveyears' course of instructionin the sub-
jectsaforesaidbeyond the qualifyingstage.

PART IX .
AFFLICTED CHILDREN .
54.-(1)The duty ofa parentunder Part VI .of this
Act to cause his childto attend school shall,in the case of
an afflictedchild as defined in this section, include the
duty to cause the childto receiveinstructionsuitableto
such child,and that duty shallcontinueinthe case of an
afflictedchilduntilthe childhas reached the age of six-
teen years, and the provisionsof the said Part VI . with
respectto the enforcement of school attendance shall
applyaccordingly.

6-
pressions" afflictedchild" and afflicted children "
mean a childor childrenbeing withinone ofthefollowing
descriptions,namely :-
(i) Blind,deaf and dumb children;that isto say,
children who are too blind to be able to read
the ordinarybooks used by the children, and
childrenwho ,by reasonofbeingdeafordumb ,
are incapableof being taught in the ordinary
classesof an elementaryschool;
(ii) Crippledchildren;
(iii) Epilepticchildren;thatistosay,childrenwho ,
not beingidiotsorimbeciles,areunfitby reason
of severeepilepsyto attend the ordinary ele-
mentary schools ;
(iv) Mentally defectivechildren,including-
(a) idiots;that isto say,childrendefec-
tive in mind from birth or from an
earlyage to such a degreeas to be un-
able to guard against common phy-
sicaldangers ;
(b) imbeciles; that isto say, childrenin
whose case there exists from birth or
from an early age mental deficiency
not amounting to idiocy, but pro-
nounced to such a degree that they are
incapableof managing themselves or
theiraffairsorofbeingtaught todo so;
(c) Feeble-minded children; that is to
say, childrenin whose case there ex-
istsfrom birth or from an early age
mental deficiencynot amounting to
imbecility,but pronounced to such a
degreethatthey requirecare,super-
visionand controlfortheirown pro-
tectionorforthe protectionofothers,
or that they, by reason of such de-
ficiency, appear to be permanently
incapableof receivingproper benefit
from the instruction afforded in or-
dinary schools,but not incapableby
reason of such deficiencyof receiving
benefitfrom instructioninsuch special
classesas may be provided under this
Act for such children .

singledistrictso assigned,and as a separateitem ofthat

mentioned authorityinprovidingtechnicalinstructionin
their education area .

subjectin any caseto any specialcovenantsor agree-

from time to time remove any of those officers.

both or all those authorities .

PART II .
EDUCATION COMMITTEES OF COUNTY BOROUGHS .
The constitution,powers,dutiesand procedureof the education
committee of a county borough,and the term of officeof the members
ofsuch educationcommittee shall,subjectto the provisionsofthisAct ,

county borough and approved by the Ministry:
Provided that-
(a) the minutes ofallmeetingsofthe educationcommittee shall
be presentedtothecouncilofthecounty borough actinginits
capacityas an educationauthority,and no actionupon those
minutes which involvesexpenditureshallbe taken by the
education committee unless and until those minutes are
approved by thecouncilactingasaforesaid;and
(b) the scheme shallmake provisionforthe appointment by the
educationcommittee of sub-committees consistingin whole
or in part of members of the educationcommittee,for the
exerciseofany ofthe powers ofthatcommittee.

SCHOOL COMMITTEES .

such schoolcommittee shall,subjectto the provisionsof thisAct ,be
such as may be determinedby the scheme,and the scheme may apply
to a schoolcommittee,withthenecessarymodifications,allorany of
the provisionsofPart I.ofthisSchedule.

CHAPTER 23 .
An Act to Provide for the making of grants in A.D.1923
aid of the repayment of certainloans and advan-
ces to rural district councils under the Labour-
ers (Ireland) Acts,1883 to 1919 .
[27th November , 1923.]
WHEREAS ,by the operationofthe Government of
IrelandAct , 1920,and the ordersmade by His Majesty
in Council thereunder, the provisionsof the Labourers
(Ireland)Acts,1883 to 1919,and ofany otherenactments
with respectto the Labourers'CottagesFund ,the Local
Taxation (Ireland) Account , the Guarantee Fund , and
the Ireland Development Grant have ceased to have
effectin Northern Ireland; and itisexpedientto make
provision,in lieuofthe saidenactments,forthe payment
out of moneys provided by Parliament of certainsums
inaid of the repayment ofloansand advances under the
said Labourers (Ireland) Acts :
B
E itthereforeenacted by the King's most Excellent
Majesty, and the Senateand the House ofCom-
mons of Northern Ireland in this present Parliament
assembled,and by theauthorityofthesame ,asfollows:-
Parliamen-
tary grants
inaidof
repaymentof loans and
advances .
1.-(1) There shallbe paid in each financialyear
outofmoneysprovidedby Parliamenttothecouncilsof
the several rural districts in Northern Ireland in
which cottages were provided under the Labourers
Acts before the commencement of the Labourers
(Ireland) Act , 1906, being cottages in respect of 6Edw.7,
which loans are for the time being outstanding,such
sums as may be certifiedto be payablein accordance
with this sub -section; and the sums so certifiedshallbe
applied towards the repayment of those loans.
The sum payable under this sub-section in any
year to the councilof a rural districtshall be a sum
equivalentto seventeen pounds per cent. of the sum

E it enacted by the King's most ExcellentMajesty,

1.-(1) The apportionment ofthe amounts payable

hundredand twenty-three, and foreachsubsequent

insteadof being made in accordance with the number of
unitsofelectricitygenerated in the precedingyear.
The expression" units of electricitysold" means
allunitsgeneratedor purchasedby a jointelectricity
authority or authorised undertaker less-
(a) those used in the generatingstation;
(b) thoselostin transmissionor distribution;and
(c) those sold in bulk to authorisedundertakers.

event of any such authority or undertaker failingto

tricityCommissioners may proceed with the apportion-

estimates .

clusiveforallpurposes :
Provided that, if it subsequently appears to the
ElectricityCommissioners that forany reasonthe appor-
tionment for any year ought to be revised, they may
revise the apportionment, and when determining the

adjustments as may be necessaryto give effectto such
revision .

[27th November , 1923.]

An Act to consolidate and amend the Law rela-
ting to Trade Boards in Northern Ireland.

[27th November , 1923.]
E itenacted by the King's Most Excellent Majesty,
and the Senate and the House of Commons of North-

by the authorityof the same ,as follows:-
APPLICATION OF ACT AND ESTABLISHMENT OF TRADE
BOARDS .

4. A Trade Board for any trade shallconsider, as
occasionrequires,any matter arisingunder thisAct which
is referredto them by the Ministry, and shallmake a
reportupon the matter to the Ministry.
A Trade Board may also,ifthey think itexpedient,
make recommendations to the Ministry,with referenceto
any such matter .
FIXING OF MINIMUM RATES .
5. Every Trade Board shallfix, for time-work in
theirtrade,minimum ratesof wages (in thisAct referred
toas"generalminimum time-rates")toapplyrespectively
to men ,women and juvenileworkers. General minimum
time-ratesshallbe fixedwithreferencetothegeneralbody
ofordinarytime-workers,keing men ,women and juvenile
workers,respectively,engaged on the leastskilledopera-
tions in the trade .
Every Trade Board shallfix,forpiece-work intheir
trade,minimum ratesofwages on a time basis(inthisActreferredto as " piece-work basistime-rates") to apply
respectivelytomen and women workers. Piece-work basis
time -rates shall be fixed with reference to workers of
ordinary skilland experienceemployed on the general
classesof piece-work operationscarriedon in the trade,
and shallbe at leastequivalentto the generalminimum
time-ratesfixedformen and women respectivelyin that
trade :

time-ratethe Ministrymay ,so far as respectsthat case,

(2)An employershall,incaseswherein-workersare
employed on piece-work and a piece-work basis time-
ratebut no general minimum piece-rate has been fixed,
be deemed to pay wages at lessthan the minimum rate,
unlesshe shows that the piece-rate of wages paid would
yield, in the circumstancesof the case, to an ordinary
worker at leastthe same amount of money as the piece-
work basis time -rate .
(3) An employer shall, in cases where out-workers
are employed on piece-work and a piece-work basistime-
ratebut no generalminimum piece-ratehas been fixed,
be deemed to pay wages at lessthan the minimum rate,
unlesshe shows that the piece-rate of wages paid would
yield, in the circumstancesof the case, to an ordinary
worker,ifperformingthework on the employer'spremises,
atleastthesame amount ofmoney asthepiece-work basis
time -rate .
(4) An employershall,inany casewhere a learner
orotherjuvenileworker isemployed on piece-work during
the firstsix months of his employment in the trade, be
deemed topay wages at lessthan the minimum rateun-
lesshe shows that such worker has received,inrespectof

## Page 213

period,at leastthe same amount of money as such worker
would have been entitledto receiveifemployed on time
work .
An employer shall, in any case where any such
worker isso employed at any time subsequent to the first
sixmonths ofhisemployment in the trade,be deemed to
pay wages at lessthan the minimum rateunlesshe shows
that such worker has, in respectof his employment on
piece-work ,been paid at piece-rateswhich would comply
with the provisionsof thisAct ifpaid to a worker (not
being a juvenileworker) employed on the same piece-
work operations.
(5) Where an offence, for which an employer is
under thisAct liableto a fine,has in fact been committed
by some agent of the employer or otherperson, that
agent or other person shallbe liableto be proceeded
against for the offence in the same manner as ifhe were
the employer, and eithertogetherwith, or beforeor
aftertheconvictionof,the employer,and shallbe liable
on convictiontothe same punishment asthattowhich the
employer isliable.
(6) Where an employer ischarged with an offence
againstthisAct , he shallbe entitled, upon information
dulylaidby him,tohave any agentorotherpersonwhom
he chargesas the actualoffenderbrought beforethe court
at the time appointed for hearing the charge ; and if,
afterthe commission of the offencehas been proved,the
employer proves to the satisfactionof the court-
(a) that he has used due diligenceto enforcethe
execution of this Act ; and
(b) that the said agent or other person had com-
mitted the offence in question without his
knowledge , consent or connivance,
that agent orotherpersonshallbe summarily convictedof
the offence, and the employer shallbe exempt from any
fineor punishment in respectof the offence, without
prejudice,however ,to the power of the court under this
sectionto adjudge him to pay any sum which appears to
the courtto be due to the person employed on account of
wages . The agent or otherperson so convictedshall, in

(7) If,at any meeting of a Trade Board ,more than
one-halfofthe members presentrepresentingthe employ-

presentingthe workers so request,the votes of the repre-
sentativemembers shallbe taken by sides, and in such
a case the vote of the majority of members of each side
presentand voting shallbe the vote of that side.
(8) A Trade Board ,may ,ifthey think fit,appoint
a committee consistingof representativesof employers
and representativesof workers, in equal numbers , being
members ofthe Board ,as the Board may choose in order
to deal in the firstinstancewith any matters as to which
the Board has powers or duties, and to report to the
Board regardingsuch matters :
Provided that, as regards the fixingof minimum
ratesof wages, the powers of any such committee shall
be advisoryonly.
(9) The Ministry may make regulationswith re-
spectto the proceedingsand meetings of Trade Boards ,

(b) disablesany such personformore than three
days from earning fullwages at the work at
which he was employed ;
written notice of the accident, in such form and accom-
paniedby suchparticularsastheMinistryofLabourmay
prescribe,shallforthwithbe sentto the inspectorforthe
district."
(2) Section one of the Notice of Accidents Act ,
1906 , so far as it relates to metalliferous mines and
quarries, shallhave effectas if for the words " and
disabledformore than seven days any person employed
in or about the mine or quarry from working at his
ordinarywork ," there were substitutedthe words " and
disabledfor more than threedays any person employed
in or about the mine or quarry from earningfullwages
at the work at which he was employed ."
(3) Paragraph (b) of sub-section (1) of section
eighteenof the Coal Mines Act, 1911, shallhave effect
as if for the words " and disabled for more than seven
days any person employed in or about the mine from
working at his ordinary work ," there were substituted
the words " and disabledfor more than three days any
person employed in or about the mine from earning
fullwages at the work at which he was employed ."
(4) This sectionshallbe construed as one with the
Notice of Accidents Act , 1906 , or the Coal Mines Act ,
1911 , as the case may require.
26.- (1) In every factorythe followingrequirements
shall have effect :-
(a) There shallbe provided and maintained so as to
be readilyaccessiblea first-aid box or cupboard
of the prescribed standard ,and where more than
one hundred and fiftypersonsare employed an
additionalbox or cupboard forevery additional
one hundred and fiftypersons.
The number of first-aid boxes or cupboards
requiredunder thisprovisionshallbe calculated
on the largestnumber of persons employed at
any one time , and fractionsof one hundred and
fiftyshallbe reckoned as one hundred and fifty.
Where the persons employed are employed in

(b) Nothing except appliancesor requisitesforfirst-

(c) Each first-aid box or cupboard shallbe placed
under the charge of a responsibleperson who
shallalways be readilyavailableduring working
hours. A noticeshallbe affixedin every work-

of the first-aid box or cupboard provided in

(d) Ifan ambulance room isprovided at the factory
and such arrangements are made as to ensure
the immediate treatment there of allinjuries

may by certificateexempt the factoryfrom the
requirements of this section to such extent and
subjectto such conditionsas itmay specifyin
the certificate;
and ifinrespectofany factorysuch requirementsarenot
complied with,the factoryshallbe deemed not to be kept
inconformitywith the Factory and Workshop Act,1901.

29.- (1) This Act may be cited as the Workmen's Shorttitleconstructi
commenceCompensation Act (Northern Ireland), 1923, and the
principalAct , the Workmen's Compensation (Anglo- mentand
FrenchConvention)Act,1909,theWorkmen'sCompen- repeal.
sation(IllegalEmployment ) Act, 1918, the Workmen's
Compensation(Silicosis)Act,1918,and thisAct may be
cited together as the Workmen's Compensation Acts
(Northern Ireland), 1906 to 1923.
(2) This Act shall, save as otherwiseexpresslypro-
vided, be construed as one with the principalAct , and
referencesin thisAct to the principalAct shallbe con-
struedas referencesto that Act as amended by thisAct .
(3) Referencesin thisAct to any Acts of the Parlia-
ment of the United Kingdom shall, unlessthe context
otherwise requires, be construed as referencesto those
Acts as they apply to Northern Ireland,under and sub-
jecttotheprovisionsoftheGovernment ofIrelandAct,
1920, and any enactments amending the same , and of
any ordermade by His MajestyinCouncilinpursuance
of the last-mentioned Act or enactments , whether made
be oreor afterthe passingofthisAct .
(4) This Act shallcome into operationon the first
day of January , nineteenhundred and twenty -four.
(5) The enactments mentioned in the Second Sche-
dule to thisAct arehereby repealedas respectsNorthern
Ireland, to the extent specifiedin the third column of
that Schedule .

SCHEDULES .
FIRST SCHEDULE .
AMENDMENTS OF SECTION 5 OF THE PRINCIPAL ACT .
1.In sub-section(1)ofsectionfiveoftheprincipalAct,afterthe
words " inthe eventofa company having commenced to be wound up,"
there shallbe insertedthe words " or a receiveror manager of the
company'sassetsby oron theapplicationofdebenture-holdershaving
been appointed ."
2. At the end of sub-section(2)of thesame sectionthereshallbe
added the words " or,as the casemay be,may recoverthebalancefrom
the receiveror manager ."
3.For sub-section(3) of the same sectionthefollowingsub-section
shall be substituted :-
" There shallbe includedamongst the debtswhich-
(i) under sectionfour of the PreferentialPayments in Bank-
ruptcy(Ireland) Act, 1889, are, in the distributionof the
propertyof a bankrupt orarrangingdebtor,to be paid in
prioritytoallother debts;
(ii) under sectiontwo hundred and nine of the Companies (Con-
solidation) Act, 1908, are inthe winding-up ofa company
to be paid inpriorityto allotherdebts;and
(iii) under sectionone hundred and seven of the Companies (Con-
solidation) Act,1908,are to be paid in priorityto any claim
forprincipalor interestin respectof debentures;
the amount due in respectof any compensation or liabilityfor
compensation accruedbeforethe followingdate,thatisto say :-
(a) in the firstcasethe date of the order of adjudicationor of
the filingof the petitionforarrangement ;
(b) in the second case the date of the commencement of the
winding-up of the company ;
(c) in the thirdcasethe date of the appointment of the receiver
or of possessionbeing taken mentioned in the said section
one hundred and seven ;
and the saidsectionsshallhave effectaccordingly.
Where the compensationisa weekly payment ,the amount due in
respectthereofshall,forthepurposesofthisprovision,be takento be
the amount ofthelump sum forwhichtheweeklypayment could, if
redeemable,be redeemed ifthe employer made an applicationfor that
purpose under the FirstScheduleto thisAct."
4. In sub-section(5)of the same sectionthe words "being wound
up " shallbe omitted .

## Page 275

LOCAL ACTS
13 & 14 GEORGE 5 .
CHAPTER i.
An Act to confer further Powers on the Belfast
City and DistrictWater Commissioners .
[22nd June , 1923.]
WHEREAS by the BelfastWater Acts 1840 to 1920
theBelfastCityand DistrictWater Commissioners(here-
inaftercalled" the Commissioners") were incorporated
and by thoseActs theirpowers were from time to time re-
gulatedand extended.
And whereas under the provisions of Sections 16 and
17 of the Belfast Water Act 1897 there are two ex -officio
Commissioners and fifteenelectiveCommissioners one for
each of fifteenWards and the electiveCommissioners are
electedin every thirdyear on the second Tuesday in the
month ofMarch forthreeyears service.
And whereas by the Local Authorities(Elections
and Constitution)Act (NorthernIreland) 1922 provision
was made for the postponement of the electionof the
fifteenelectiveCommissionersuntilthe secondTuesday
in the month of March 1924 .
And whereas itisexpedientto alterthe constitution
of the Commissioners so that one thirdofthe electiveCom-
missionersshallgo out ofofficeineach year.
And whereas it isexpedient to make provisionfor
the consent of candidates to nomination for electionand
for the payment of a money depositby them on nomi-
nation .
And whereas itisexpedientthat the Commissioners
and theirofficersshould be required to make a declaration
of allegiancesimilarto that requiredof members and
officersof Local Authoritiesby the Local Government
Act (NorthernIreland)1922.
A.D. 1

## Page 276

of the Commissioners isthe Local Government Register
fortheCounty Borough ofBelfasttogetherwith aSupple-
mental Registerof electorsforthe Suburban Districtsin
the Commissioners area of supply and is dividedinto
fifteen Wards .
And whereas by Section7 ofthe Local Government
Act (Northern Ireland)1922 the MinistryofHome Affairs
may from time to time make ordersalteringthe number-
and boundariesofthe Wards of the County Borough and
it is expedient that furtherprovisionshould be made
authorisingthe saidMinistryto make Orders forthepur-
pose ofmaking theRegisterofLocalGovernment Electors
for the County Borough and Suburban Districtsavail-
ableforthepurposesofelectionofCommissioners.
And whereas itisexpedientto make provisionfor
includingintheproperWard intheSupplemental Registe
ofElectorsthe name ofany person who isa localgovern-
ment elector in the Suburban Districts where such elector
isnot includedin the same Ward in the registerof loca
government electorsforthe County Borough .
And whereas itisexpedientto authorisethe Com
missionersto borrow money by the issueofBills.
And whereas the Commissioners have acquired land
which can be sold or let without detriment to their under
takingand itisexpedientthat the Commissioners shoul
be authorisedto selland letsuch lands as inthisAct pro
vided .
And whereas it is expedient to make provisio

CHAPTER iii.
An Act to confirm a Provisional Order of the
Ministry of Home Affairsfor Northern Ireland
relating to the Urban District of Bangor .
[22nd June , 1923.]
WHEREASHEREAStheMinistryofHomeAffairsforNorth-
ern Ireland has made the Provisional Order set
out in the Schedule hereto under the Public Health
(Ireland) Acts, 1878 to 1919 :
AND WHEREAS itisrequisitethat the said Order
should be confirmed by Parliament :
Be itthereforeenactedby theKing'smost Excellent
Majesty, and the Senate and the House of Commons of
Northern Ireland in thispresent Parliament assembled,
and by the authorityof the same ,as follows:--
1. The Order set out in the Schedule hereto shall be
and the same ishereby confirmed,and allthe provisions
thereofshallhave fullvalidityand force.
2. ThisAct may be citedas theBangor Gas Pro-
visionalOrder ConfirmationAct (Northern Ireland),
1923 .

:
An Act to empower The Right Honourable the
Lord Mayor Aldermen and Citizens of the City
of Belfast to construct and work Additional
Tramways within and outside the City and to
execute certain Works ; To confer further
powers upon the Corporation with referenceto
theirGas Undertaking and in relationto Public
Health and Sanitary Matters and to the Good
Government ofthe City ;and forother purposes.
[22nd June , 1923.]
WHEREAS the cityof Belfast(in thisAct called
"the city") isa county borough subjectto the Acts
relatingto municipal corporationsin Northern Ireland
and The Right Honourable the Lord Mayor Aldermen
and CitizensoftheCity(inthisAct called" theCorpora-
tion") actingby the Councilare the urban sanitary
authorityfor the districtthereof:
And whereas the several local Acts and Orders
mentioned in the First Schedule to this Act are in force
within the citywhich Acts and Orders are in thisActreferredto collectivelyas " the former Acts " and each of
them separatelyas an Act or Order of the year in which
the same was passed or made :
And whereas under powers ofcertainof the former
Acts the Corporationare the owners of and are working
the tramway system of the cityand itisexpedientthat
the Corporationshould be empowered to construct
furthertramways withinand without the City as by this
Act authorised :
And whereas it is expedient that the Corporation
should be authorised to make the street works in this Act
describedand to exerciseinrelationtheretothe powers by
this Act conferred :
And whereas it isexpedient that the Corporation
should be authorisedto acquirecertainlands known as
" Hazelwood " and lay out and equip the same as a Park
or recreationground :
And whereas it isexpedient that the Corporation
shouldbe empowered toacquireholdand dealwithlands
for the purposes of thisAct and to sellexchange letor
otherwisedisposeofsuch landsas may be acquiredforor

6. The Tramways shallbe constructedon a gauge
offourfeeteightand a-halfinchesand carriagesortrucks
adapted to run on railwaysshallnot be used thereon.
7. If the Tramways be not completed and opened
forpublictrafficwithinfiveyearsfrom the passingofthis
Act then on the expirationof that periodthe powers by
thisAct granted for constructingthe same or otherwise
in relationtheretoshallceaseexcept as to so much ofthe
Tramways as shallthen be completed.
8. Subjectto the provisionsof thisAct the Tram-
ways shallforallpurposesbe deemed to form part ofthe
Tramway Undertaking and ofthe CorporationTramways .
9. No part of the Tramways shallbe opened for
publictrafficuntilithas been inspectedand certifiedtobe
fitforsuchtrafficby an officerappointedby theMinistry
of Home Affairs.
10. No post or other apparatus for working the
Tramways shallbe erectedon the carriagewayof any
streetor road except with the consent of the Ministryof
Home Affairs .

railwayand so that the top of any such pipe or other
work shallnot in any case be nearerthe bottom of the
railsof the railwaythan 3 feetor such lesserdepth that
the Railway Company may require.
(2) In laying and maintaining any other mains
pipesculvertsor otherworks (hereinafterincludedinthe
expression " the authorisedworks ") over upon across

reasonablesatisfactionof the Engineer of the Railway
Company and in accordance with plans sectionsand
specificationspreviouslysubmitted to and approved by
him .

any levelcrossingof such railwayor over the approaches
to any such bridge so faras the same may be disturbed
or interferedwith by or inconnectionwith the authorised
works .

in connection therewith .
